Most likely the\n    expression is a Lookup instance.\n\n    However, a child could also be any class with as_sql() and either\n    relabeled_clone() method or relabel_aliases() and clone() methods and\n    contains_aggregate attribute.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    default = AND\n    resolved = False\n    conditional = True\n\n    def split_having_qualify(self, negated=False, must_group_by=False):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return three possibly None nodes: one for those parts of self that\n        should be included in the WHERE clause, one for those parts of self\n        that must be included in the HAVING clause, and one for those parts\n        that refer to window functions.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self.contains_aggregate and not self.contains_over_clause:\n            return self, None, None\n        in_negated = negated ^ self.negated\n        # It's must cheaper to short-circuit and stash everything in the\n            # HAVING clause than split children if possible.\n            return None, self, None\n        where_parts = []\n        having_parts = []\n        qualify_parts = []\n        for c in self.children:\n            if hasattr(c, \"split_having_qualify\"):\n                where_part, having_part, qualify_part = c.split_having_qualify(\n                    in_negated, must_group_by\n                )\n                if where_part is not None:\n                    where_parts.append(where_part)\n                if having_part is not None:\n                    having_parts.append(having_part)\n                if qualify_part is not None:\n                    qualify_parts.append(qualify_part)\n            elif c.contains_over_clause:\n                qualify_parts.append(c)\n            elif c.contains_aggregate:\n                having_parts.append(c)\n            else:\n                where_parts.append(c)\n        if must_remain_connected and qualify_parts:\n            # Disjunctive heterogeneous predicates can be pushed down to\n            # qualify as long as no conditional aggregation is involved.\n            if not where_parts or (where_parts and not must_group_by):\n                return None, None, self\n            elif where_parts:\n                # In theory this should only be enforced when dealing with\n                # where_parts containing predicates against multi-valued\n                # relationships that could affect aggregation results but this\n                # is complex to infer properly.\n                raise NotImplementedError(\n                    \"Heterogeneous disjunctive predicates against window functions are \"\n                    \"not implemented when performing conditional aggregation.\"\n                )\n        where_node = (\n            self.create(where_parts, self.connector, self.negated)\n            if where_parts\n            else None\n        )\n        having_node = (\n            self.create(having_parts, self.connector, self.negated)\n            if having_parts\n            else None\n        )\n        qualify_node = (\n            self.create(qualify_parts, self.connector, self.negated)\n            if qualify_parts\n            else None\n        )\n        return where_node, having_node, qualify_node\n\n    def as_sql(self, compiler, connection):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the SQL version of the where clause and the value to be\n        substituted in. Return '', [] if this node matches everything,\n        None, [] if this node is empty, and raise EmptyResultSet if this\n        node can't match anything.\n        \"\"\"\n        result = []\n        result_params = []\n        if self.connector == AND:\n            full_needed, empty_needed = len(self.children), 1\n        else:\n            full_needed, empty_needed = 1, len(self.children)\n\n        if self.connector == XOR and not connection.features.supports_logical_xor:\n            # Convert if the database doesn't support XOR:\n            #   a XOR b XOR c XOR ...\n            # to:\n            #   (a OR b OR c OR ...) AND MOD(a + b + c + ..., 2) == 1\n            # The result of an n-ary XOR is true when an odd number of operands\n            # are true.\n            lhs = self.__class__(self.children, OR)\n            rhs_sum = reduce(\n                operator.add,\n                (Case(When(c, then=1), default=0) for c in self.children),\n            )\n            if len(self.children) > 2:\n                rhs_sum = Mod(rhs_sum, 2)\n            rhs = Exact(1, rhs_sum)\n            return self.__class__([lhs, rhs], AND, self.negated).as_sql(\n                compiler, connection\n            )\n\n        for child in self.children:\n            try:\n                sql, params = compiler.compile(child)\n            except EmptyResultSet:\n                empty_needed -= 1\n            except FullResultSet:\n                full_needed -= 1\n            else:\n                if sql:\n                    result.append(sql)\n                    result_params.extend(params)\n                else:\n                    full_needed -= 1\n            # Check if this node matches nothing or everything.\n            # First check the amount of full nodes and empty nodes\n            # to make this node empty/full.\n            # Now, check if this node is full/empty using the\n            # counts.\n            if empty_needed == 0:\n                if self.negated:\n                    raise FullResultSet\n                else:\n                    raise EmptyResultSet\n            if full_needed == 0:\n                if self.negated:\n                    raise EmptyResultSet\n                else:\n                    raise FullResultSet\n        conn = \" %s \" % self.connector\n        sql_string = conn.join(result)\n        if not sql_string:\n            raise FullResultSet\n        if self.negated:\n            # `as_sql()` iterates children via `compiler.compile()`; `split_having_qualify()` for HAVING/QUALIFY clauses; `NothingNode`, `ExtraWhere`\n- `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `SQLCompiler` and subclasses (`SQLInsertCompiler`, `SQLUpdateCompiler`, `SQLDeleteCompiler`, `SQLAggregateCompiler`); `compile()` vendor dispatch; `as_sql()` assembles full SQL; `execute_sql()` runs the query\n- `django/db/models/sql/subqueries.py` — Specialized `Query` subclasses (`DeleteQuery`, `UpdateQuery`, `InsertQuery`, `AggregateQuery`) each declaring a `compiler` class attribute naming which compiler class to use\n- `django/db/models/sql/datastructures.py` — `Join`, `BaseTable`, `MultiJoin` data structures for alias/join tracking in the Query\n- `django/db/models/sql/constants.py` — Shared constants (`INNER`, `LOUTER`, `SINGLE`, `MULTI`, `CURSOR`, `ORDER_DIR`, etc.)\n- `django/db/models/expressions.py` — `BaseExpression` (Expression protocol: `as_sql`, `resolve_expression`, `get_source_expressions`); `Col`, `F`, `Value`, `Ref`, `RawSQL`, `Exists`, `CombinedExpression`, `Window`, `Case`/`When`, etc.; `Combinable` mixin for arithmetic operators; `SQLiteNumericMixin` for vendor overrides\n- `django/db/models/lookups.py` — `Lookup(Expression)` base class; `Transform`; `BuiltinLookup`; concrete lookups (`Exact`, `GreaterThan`, `In`, `IsNull`, etc.); `process_lhs()`/`process_rhs()` to compile each side\n- `django/db/models/aggregates.py` — Aggregate expressions (`Count`, `Sum`, `Avg`, etc.) extending `Func`/`Expression`; produce SQL aggregate functions\n- `django/db/models/fields/__init__.py` — `Field` inherits `RegisterLookupMixin`; registers lookups (`exact`, `in`, `lt`, `gt`, etc.) at class level; `get_db_prep_value()` converts Python values to DB-ready form\n- `django/db/backends/base/operations.py` — `BaseDatabaseOperations`; `compiler_module = \"django.db.models.sql.compiler\"` default; `compiler(name)` factory returns the named compiler class from the module; `lookup_cast()`, `operators` dict, quote utilities\n- `django/db/backends/base/features.py` — `BaseDatabaseFeatures`; boolean capability flags (`supports_logical_xor`, `allows_group_by_selected_pks`, `supports_boolean_expr_in_select_clause`, etc.) consulted during SQL assembly\n- `django/db/backends/mysql/operations.py` — `DatabaseOperations` overrides `compiler_module = \"django.db.backends.mysql.compiler\"` to route to MySQL-specific compiler\n- `django/db/backends/mysql/compiler.py` — MySQL-specific `SQLDeleteCompiler` (DELETE … FROM multi-table syntax) and `SQLUpdateCompiler` (UPDATE … ORDER BY support)\n- `django/db/backends/postgresql/operations.py` — `DatabaseOperations` overrides `compiler_module = \"django.db.backends.postgresql.compiler\"`\n- `django/db/backends/postgresql/compiler.py` — PostgreSQL-specific `SQLInsertCompiler` using UNNEST for bulk inserts\n- `django/db/backends/sqlite3/operations.py` — SQLite operations (no separate compiler module override; uses base compiler)\n- `django/db/backends/oracle/operations.py` — Oracle operations; lookups/expressions may define `as_oracle()` methods for compatibility\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `django/db/models/manager.py` — `Manager.get_queryset()` instantiates `QuerySet(model=self.model, using=self._db, hints=self._hints)`; Manager methods (filter, exclude, etc.) are dynamically proxied via `_get_queryset_methods()` to delegate to the QuerySet\n\n2. **QuerySet lazy filter construction**: `django/db/models/query.py` — `QuerySet.filter(*args, **kwargs)` calls `_filter_or_exclude(False, args, kwargs)` which chains a copy and calls `_filter_or_exclude_inplace()` → `self._query.add_q(Q(*args, **kwargs))`; no SQL is generated yet\n\n3. **Q object composition**: `django/db/models/query_utils.py` — `Q` (a `tree.Node` subclass) stores filter kwargs as `(key, value)` children; supports `&`, `|`, `^`, `~` operators producing nested Q trees with AND/OR/XOR/negated connectors\n\n4. **Query WHERE tree construction**: `django/db/models/sql/query.py`:\n   - `Query.add_q(q_object)` → determines reusable aliases → calls `_add_q(q_object, can_reuse)` → attaches result clause to `self.where` with `self.where.add(clause, AND)`\n   - `Query._add_q(q_object, used_aliases)` → creates a `WhereNode` with the Q object's connector/negated flags → iterates over `q_object.children` → calls `build_filter(child, ...)` for each → adds resulting child clauses into `target_clause`\n   - `Query.build_filter(filter_expr)` → calls `solve_lookup_type(arg)` to split `\"field__lookup\"` strings into field traversal parts and lookup names → calls `setup_joins(parts, opts, alias)` to compute JOINs → resolves the RHS value → calls `build_lookup(lookups, lhs, rhs)` → returns a `WhereNode([lookup])`\n   - `Query.build_lookup(lookups, lhs, rhs)` → applies any Transform chain (e.g. `date`, `year`) via `try_transform()` → calls `lhs.get_lookup(lookup_name)` (via `RegisterLookupMixin`) → instantiates `lookup_class(lhs, rhs)` → returns a `Lookup` node\n\n5. **Lookup resolution**: `django/db/models/lookups.py` — `Lookup.__init__` calls `get_prep_lookup()` to prepare the RHS value (via `Field.get_prep_value()`) and `get_prep_lhs()`\n\n6. **WhereNode tree**: `django/db/models/sql/where.py` — `WhereNode` accumulates `Lookup` leaf nodes and nested `WhereNode` sub-trees connected by AND/OR/XOR operators; this tree is stored on `Query.where`\n\n7. **Evaluation trigger**: `django/db/models/query.py` — Iteration (`__iter__`), `len()`, boolean coercion, indexing all call `_fetch_all()` → `_iterator()` → `ModelIterable.__iter__()`\n\n8. **Compiler creation**: `django/db/models/query.py` (`ModelIterable.__iter__`) → `queryset.query.get_compiler(using=db)` which calls `django/db/models/sql/query.py`:\n   - `Query.get_compiler(using)` → `connection = connections[using]` → `connection.ops.compiler(self.compiler)(self, connection, using, elide_empty)`\n   - `BaseDatabaseOperations.compiler(compiler_name)` (in `django/db/backends/base/operations.py`) → `import_module(self.compiler_module)` → `getattr(module, compiler_name)`; backends override `compiler_module` to inject backend-specific compiler classes\n\n9. **SQL assembly**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `SQLCompiler.execute_sql()` calls `self.as_sql()`:\n   - `as_sql()` → `pre_sql_setup()` (resolves SELECT columns, ORDER BY, splits WHERE into where/having/qualify) → assembles `SELECT … FROM … WHERE … GROUP BY … HAVING … ORDER BY …` strings\n   - `compile(self.where)` is called to render the WHERE clause via `WhereNode.as_sql()`\n\n10. **Vendor dispatch**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `SQLCompiler.compile(node)`:\n    ```python\n    def compile(self, node):\n        vendor_impl = getattr(node, \"as_\" + self.connection.vendor, None)\n        if vendor_impl:\n            sql, params = vendor_impl(self, self.connection)\n        else:\n            sql, params = node.as_sql(self, self.connection)\n        return sql, params\n    ```\n    Checks for `as_postgresql`, `as_mysql`, `as_sqlite`, `as_oracle` on the node before falling back to `as_sql`.\n\n11. **WhereNode SQL rendering**: `django/db/models/sql/where.py` — `WhereNode.as_sql(compiler, connection)` iterates children and calls `compiler.compile(child)` on each, collecting `(sql, params)` pairs, joining them with the connector (`AND`/`OR`/`XOR`), wrapping in `NOT (…)` if negated\n\n12. **Lookup SQL rendering**: `django/db/models/lookups.py` — `BuiltinLookup.as_sql(compiler, connection)` calls `process_lhs(compiler, connection)` and `process_rhs(compiler, connection)`, which in turn call `compiler.compile(lhs_expr)` and `compiler.compile(rhs_expr)`; then formats using `connection.operators[lookup_name]`\n\n13. **Execution**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `execute_sql()` obtains a cursor via `self.connection.cursor()`, calls `cursor.execute(sql, params)`, and returns results based on `result_type` (MULTI/SINGLE/CURSOR/ROW_COUNT)\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n**Lazy Evaluation (Virtual Proxy)**\nQuerySet objects are lazy: every call to `filter()`, `exclude()`, `annotate()`, `order_by()` etc. clones the QuerySet and mutates the underlying `Query` object (a pure Python data structure) without touching the database. SQL generation and database execution are deferred until the result set is actually consumed (iteration, `len()`, slicing to a list, `bool()`, etc.). This is the defining architectural characteristic of the ORM.\n\n**Composite Pattern (WhereNode)**\n`WhereNode` (from `django/utils/tree.Node`) is a composite tree. Leaf nodes are `Lookup` instances (boolean SQL expressions), and interior nodes are `WhereNode` instances with `AND`, `OR`, or `XOR` connectors and an optional `negated` flag. This tree exactly mirrors the logical structure of the user's filter expressions, including nested `Q(…) | Q(…)` combinations. `WhereNode.as_sql()` recursively renders the tree bottom-up.\n\n**Visitor Pattern (compile dispatch)**\n`SQLCompiler` acts as a visitor. Its `compile(node)` method accepts any expression node and dispatches to `node.as_sql(compiler, connection)`. The compiler is passed as an argument to every `as_sql()` call, enabling each node to compile its sub-expressions by calling back into `compiler.compile(sub_node)`. This mutual recursion (compiler→node→compiler→node) is how arbitrarily nested expressions are rendered to SQL.\n\n**Strategy Pattern (vendor dispatch)**\nThe `compile()` method implements a two-level strategy pattern. First, it checks for a vendor-specific method (`as_postgresql`, `as_mysql`, `as_sqlite`, `as_oracle`) on each node. This allows individual expression or lookup classes to override their SQL generation for specific backends without subclassing the compiler. Second, `BaseDatabaseOperations.compiler_module` is overridden per backend (MySQL sets it to `django.db.backends.mysql.compiler`) to load backend-specific compiler subclasses, allowing whole-compiler overrides (e.g., MySQL's multi-table `DELETE … FROM` syntax).\n\n**Template Method (Query/Compiler hierarchy)**\n`SQLCompiler.as_sql()` is a template method: it calls `pre_sql_setup()`, `get_from_clause()`, `get_order_by()`, `get_group_by()`, and `compile(self.where)` in a fixed sequence to assemble the SQL string. Backend subclasses (e.g., `SQLDeleteCompiler` for MySQL) override specific parts of this assembly without changing the overall flow.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `Manager` | Entry point; namespace for `objects`; creates QuerySet |\n| `QuerySet` | Public ORM API; lazy container; delegates filter logic to `Query` |\n| `Q` | User-facing composable filter node; maps to `WhereNode` structure |\n| `Query` | SQL data structure; manages aliases, joins, WHERE tree, annotations |\n| `WhereNode` | Composite boolean tree; renders to SQL recursively |\n| `Lookup` | Leaf SQL boolean expression; compiles LHS op RHS |\n| `Transform` | Chained field transformation (e.g., `date`, `year`, `lower`) |\n| `BaseExpression` / `Expression` | Protocol base for all SQL-generatable nodes |\n| `RegisterLookupMixin` | Lookup registry on Field and Expression classes |\n| `SQLCompiler` | Assembles full SELECT SQL; vendor dispatch hub |\n| `BaseDatabaseOperations` | Backend capability/behavior abstraction; compiler factory |\n| `BaseDatabaseFeatures` | Boolean feature flags consulted during SQL assembly |\n\n### Data Flow\n\n```\nModel.objects.filter(name__startswith=\"A\", age__gt=18)\n        │\n        ▼\nManager.get_queryset()                          # Creates QuerySet\n        │\n        ▼\nQuerySet.filter(...)                            # Returns cloned QuerySet (no SQL)\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nQuery.add_q(Q(name__startswith=\"A\", age__gt=18))\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nQuery._add_q(q_object)                          # Iterates Q children\n        │  for each child, calls\n        ▼\nQuery.build_filter((\"name__startswith\", \"A\"))\n        │  calls solve_lookup_type → [\"startswith\"], [\"name\"]\n        │  calls setup_joins → computes alias for \"name\" column\n        │  calls build_lookup([\"startswith\"], Col(\"name\"), \"A\")\n        │         → lhs.get_lookup(\"startswith\") → StartsWithLookup\n        │         → StartsWithLookup(Col(\"name\"), \"A\")\n        ▼\nWhereNode([StartsWithLookup, GreaterThanLookup], connector=AND)\n        │  stored on Query.where\n        │\n        ▼  (when iteration is triggered)\nModelIterable.__iter__()\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nQuery.get_compiler(using=\"default\")\n        │  → connection.ops.compiler(\"SQLCompiler\")(query, connection, ...)\n        ▼\nSQLCompiler.execute_sql()\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nSQLCompiler.as_sql()\n        │  calls compile(self.where)\n        ▼\nWhereNode.as_sql(compiler, connection)\n        │  for each child, calls compiler.compile(child)\n        ▼\nSQLCompiler.compile(StartsWithLookup)\n        │  → checks for as_postgresql/as_mysql/etc. → falls back to as_sql()\n        ▼\nStartsWithLookup.as_sql(compiler, connection)\n        │  → process_lhs → compiler.compile(Col(\"name\")) → \"app_table\".\"name\"\n        │  → process_rhs → get_db_prep_lookup → \"%A%\"\n        │  → returns (\"\\\"app_table\\\".\\\"name\\\" LIKE %s\", [\"A%\"])\n        ▼\ncursor.execute(\"SELECT ... FROM app_table WHERE \\\"name\\\" LIKE %s AND \\\"age\\\" > %s\", [\"A%\", 18])\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n**Expression Protocol**: Any object that participates in SQL generation must implement:\n- `as_sql(compiler, connection) → (str, list)` — returns SQL fragment and parameter list\n- `resolve_expression(query, allow_joins, reuse, summarize, for_save) → Expression` — resolves field references, validates, and returns a self-contained expression\n- `get_source_expressions() → list` — for traversal/copying of sub-expressions\n- `set_source_expressions(exprs)` — for mutation during resolution\n\n**Lookup Contract**: Lookups additionally implement:\n- `process_lhs(compiler, connection) → (str, list)` — compile the left-hand side\n- `process_rhs(compiler, connection) → (str, list)` — compile the right-hand side\n- `get_db_prep_lookup(value, connection) → (\"%s\", [prepared_value])` — prepare value for DB driver\n\n**Compiler Contract** (what nodes expect of the compiler):\n- `compiler.compile(node) → (str, list)` — the only method nodes call back into\n- `compiler.connection` — access to backend connection/features/ops\n- `compiler.query` — access to the Query object\n\n**Backend Dispatch Contract**: `compile(node)` performs `getattr(node, \"as_\" + connection.vendor, None)`; if an expression class defines `as_sqlite`, `as_postgresql`, etc., it overrides the default `as_sql()` for that backend without any explicit registration.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Django ORM query compilation pipeline is a two-phase lazy system: the **construction phase** (triggered by `filter()`, `exclude()`, etc.) builds an in-memory `Query` object containing a `WhereNode` composite tree of `Lookup` and nested `WhereNode` nodes, with no database interaction. The **compilation phase** (triggered by iteration or other evaluation) uses `SQLCompiler` — selected via `BaseDatabaseOperations.compiler_module` for backend-specific routing — which renders the WHERE tree to SQL by recursively dispatching through `compile(node)`, which first checks for vendor-specific `as_{vendor}()` methods before falling back to `as_sql()`, enabling expression-level backend customization. This architecture cleanly separates query construction (Query/WhereNode), SQL generation (SQLCompiler/Expression protocol), and backend adaptation (vendor dispatch + compiler subclasses), making the ORM both database-agnostic and extensible at every layer.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":110,"cache_read_input_tokens":66840,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":110,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":21,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"99969201-7b95-4f4d-a783-085596b0b532","uuid":"6fd16854-6283-416b-b08a-9c58a0992869"}

then formats using `connection.operators[lookup_name]`\n\n13. **Execution**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `execute_sql()` obtains a cursor via `self.connection.cursor()`, calls `cursor.execute(sql, params)`, and returns results based on `result_type` (MULTI/SINGLE/CURSOR/ROW_COUNT)\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n**Lazy Evaluation (Virtual Proxy)**\nQuerySet objects are lazy: every call to `filter()`, `exclude()`, `annotate()`, `order_by()` etc. clones the QuerySet and mutates the underlying `Query` object (a pure Python data structure) without touching the database. SQL generation and database execution are deferred until the result set is actually consumed (iteration, `len()`, slicing to a list, `bool()`, etc.). This is the defining architectural characteristic of the ORM.\n\n**Composite Pattern (WhereNode)**\n`WhereNode` (from `django/utils/tree.Node`) is a composite tree. Leaf nodes are `Lookup` instances (boolean SQL expressions), and interior nodes are `WhereNode` instances with `AND`, `OR`, or `XOR` connectors and an optional `negated` flag. This tree exactly mirrors the logical structure of the user's filter expressions, including nested `Q(…) | Q(…)` combinations. `WhereNode.as_sql()` recursively renders the tree bottom-up.\n\n**Visitor Pattern (compile dispatch)**\n`SQLCompiler` acts as a visitor. Its `compile(node)` method accepts any expression node and dispatches to `node.as_sql(compiler, connection)`. The compiler is passed as an argument to every `as_sql()` call, enabling each node to compile its sub-expressions by calling back into `compiler.compile(sub_node)`. This mutual recursion (compiler→node→compiler→node) is how arbitrarily nested expressions are rendered to SQL.\n\n**Strategy Pattern (vendor dispatch)**\nThe `compile()` method implements a two-level strategy pattern. First, it checks for a vendor-specific method (`as_postgresql`, `as_mysql`, `as_sqlite`, `as_oracle`) on each node. This allows individual expression or lookup classes to override their SQL generation for specific backends without subclassing the compiler. Second, `BaseDatabaseOperations.compiler_module` is overridden per backend (MySQL sets it to `django.db.backends.mysql.compiler`) to load backend-specific compiler subclasses, allowing whole-compiler overrides (e.g., MySQL's multi-table `DELETE … FROM` syntax).\n\n**Template Method (Query/Compiler hierarchy)**\n`SQLCompiler.as_sql()` is a template method: it calls `pre_sql_setup()`, `get_from_clause()`, `get_order_by()`, `get_group_by()`, and `compile(self.where)` in a fixed sequence to assemble the SQL string. Backend subclasses (e.g., `SQLDeleteCompiler` for MySQL) override specific parts of this assembly without changing the overall flow.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `Manager` | Entry point; namespace for `objects`; creates QuerySet |\n| `QuerySet` | Public ORM API; lazy container; delegates filter logic to `Query` |\n| `Q` | User-facing composable filter node; maps to `WhereNode` structure |\n| `Query` | SQL data structure; manages aliases, joins, WHERE tree, annotations |\n| `WhereNode` | Composite boolean tree; renders to SQL recursively |\n| `Lookup` | Leaf SQL boolean expression; compiles LHS op RHS |\n| `Transform` | Chained field transformation (e.g., `date`, `year`, `lower`) |\n| `BaseExpression` / `Expression` | Protocol base for all SQL-generatable nodes |\n| `RegisterLookupMixin` | Lookup registry on Field and Expression classes |\n| `SQLCompiler` | Assembles full SELECT SQL; vendor dispatch hub |\n| `BaseDatabaseOperations` | Backend capability/behavior abstraction; compiler factory |\n| `BaseDatabaseFeatures` | Boolean feature flags consulted during SQL assembly |\n\n### Data Flow\n\n```\nModel.objects.filter(name__startswith=\"A\", age__gt=18)\n        │\n        ▼\nManager.get_queryset()                          # Creates QuerySet\n        │\n        ▼\nQuerySet.filter(...)                            # Returns cloned QuerySet (no SQL)\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nQuery.add_q(Q(name__startswith=\"A\", age__gt=18))\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nQuery._add_q(q_object)                          # Iterates Q children\n        │  for each child, calls\n        ▼\nQuery.build_filter((\"name__startswith\", \"A\"))\n        │  calls solve_lookup_type → [\"startswith\"], [\"name\"]\n        │  calls setup_joins → computes alias for \"name\" column\n        │  calls build_lookup([\"startswith\"], Col(\"name\"), \"A\")\n        │         → lhs.get_lookup(\"startswith\") → StartsWithLookup\n        │         → StartsWithLookup(Col(\"name\"), \"A\")\n        ▼\nWhereNode([StartsWithLookup, GreaterThanLookup], connector=AND)\n        │  stored on Query.where\n        │\n        ▼  (when iteration is triggered)\nModelIterable.__iter__()\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nQuery.get_compiler(using=\"default\")\n        │  → connection.ops.compiler(\"SQLCompiler\")(query, connection, ...)\n        ▼\nSQLCompiler.execute_sql()\n        │  calls\n        ▼\nSQLCompiler.as_sql()\n        │  calls compile(self.where)\n        ▼\nWhereNode.as_sql(compiler, connection)\n        │  for each child, calls compiler.compile(child)\n        ▼\nSQLCompiler.compile(StartsWithLookup)\n        │  → checks for as_postgresql/as_mysql/etc. → falls back to as_sql()\n        ▼\nStartsWithLookup.as_sql(compiler, connection)\n        │  → process_lhs → compiler.compile(Col(\"name\")) → \"app_table\".\"name\"\n        │  → process_rhs → get_db_prep_lookup → \"%A%\"\n        │  → returns (\"\\\"app_table\\\".\\\"name\\\" LIKE %s\", [\"A%\"])\n        ▼\ncursor.execute(\"SELECT ... FROM app_table WHERE \\\"name\\\" LIKE %s AND \\\"age\\\" > %s\", [\"A%\", 18])\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n**Expression Protocol**: Any object that participates in SQL generation must implement:\n- `as_sql(compiler, connection) → (str, list)` — returns SQL fragment and parameter list\n- `resolve_expression(query, allow_joins, reuse, summarize, for_save) → Expression` — resolves field references, validates, and returns a self-contained expression\n- `get_source_expressions() → list` — for traversal/copying of sub-expressions\n- `set_source_expressions(exprs)` — for mutation during resolution\n\n**Lookup Contract**: Lookups additionally implement:\n- `process_lhs(compiler, connection) → (str, list)` — compile the left-hand side\n- `process_rhs(compiler, connection) → (str, list)` — compile the right-hand side\n- `get_db_prep_lookup(value, connection) → (\"%s\", [prepared_value])` — prepare value for DB driver\n\n**Compiler Contract** (what nodes expect of the compiler):\n- `compiler.compile(node) → (str, list)` — the only method nodes call back into\n- `compiler.connection` — access to backend connection/features/ops\n- `compiler.query` — access to the Query object\n\n**Backend Dispatch Contract**: `compile(node)` performs `getattr(node, \"as_\" + connection.vendor, None)`; if an expression class defines `as_sqlite`, `as_postgresql`, etc., it overrides the default `as_sql()` for that backend without any explicit registration.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Django ORM query compilation pipeline is a two-phase lazy system: the **construction phase** (triggered by `filter()`, `exclude()`, etc.) builds an in-memory `Query` object containing a `WhereNode` composite tree of `Lookup` and nested `WhereNode` nodes, with no database interaction. The **compilation phase** (triggered by iteration or other evaluation) uses `SQLCompiler` — selected via `BaseDatabaseOperations.compiler_module` for backend-specific routing — which renders the WHERE tree to SQL by recursively dispatching through `compile(node)`, which first checks for vendor-specific `as_{vendor}()` methods before falling back to `as_sql()`, enabling expression-level backend customization. This architecture cleanly separates query construction (Query/WhereNode), SQL generation (SQLCompiler/Expression protocol), and backend adaptation (vendor dispatch + compiler subclasses), making the ORM both database-agnostic and extensible at every layer.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
